The main problem here is authenticity of the food and the care that is taken in providing it. It may not be understood by all, but when a key aspect of your culture is not properly showcased it is discomforting and reduces patriotism. I was told that CaribSAand the MRC requested Jerked chicken and Rice & Beans for Caribbean Night. What they served there was uncooked curried rice and peas with carrots and chicken which don\u2019t even resemble anything close to jerked chicken. \nAnother instance, for Indian students Fresher\u2019s party one time, I unfortunately happened to eat Chicken Biriyani. But the one I had which was cooked by Sodexo, it happened to be plain rice and dry chicken. So here Sodexo [at TAMU-Commerce] has been constantly proving that, it\u2019s not their cup of tea to cook international food. Well, business being one of my major at the masters level, if I were a part of Sodexo\u00ae corporaion, I would stand for making more business for them and the bottom-line for business is customer service, customer relations, and repeat business. If the emphasis is on money, that business will not have longevity. Sodexo\u00ae will be around for a while because they are one of the Big Three university dining services that have monopolized the industry. I don\u2019t understand why a state institution like Texas A&M university- Commerce is keenly interested in helping Sodexo to make profits especially through non-profit student organizations and urging fundraising to pay high price for meals is ridiculous. We are willing to pay a little more for convenience and quality service to highlight our authentic cultural food, but are also not financially foolish. Why pay three times for something we could get else where at a much lower cost? Supply and demand is what should be of concern here, not the need to make a bundle of money off student\u2019s organization. After all, the building we cannot use to host these events are paid for by the high student\u2019s fee made possible by alumni and current students. Should we make that contribution, be inconvenienced, and chased out? What are the needs of the campus? Isn\u2019t that what we have been voicing and they have been ignored? Therefore mean profit is being made, but the needs of the campus [students] are not being met. \nAs said in the article by Wendy, that \u201cstudent organizations should do fundraising\u201d. Bake sale is one of the most profitable ways of fundraising in terms of raw material and cost of goods sold. From this spring semester, all the student organizations cannot do the bake sale inside the student center unless we get the bale sale stuff from Sodexo. When I checked the Sodexo price list, assorted cookies cost $4.99 for a dozen. That means it would cost $0.40 for a cookie. Let\u2019s say Charles works with us and price a cookie for $0.30 and we ordered 100 cookies and sell it for $1 (which is already asking too much). Then the profit we make is $0.70. The programs we international students host, are expecting at least 250 \u2013 300 people which includes the members, other students, alumni, faculty and Commerce community. If we get food from Sodexo, what I have seen is that they would charge at least $12 per head without catering, which would cost $3,600 for 300 people just for food. We have to sell 5,142 cookies to cover just the cost of the food for the event. Since SOAC has a cap of $1500 per organization per event, and say they would pay for food if approved, then again we have to pay $2,100. So where can we get money for the decorations and entertainment etc. being that we are a non-profit organization? These are from my experience being a Vice President for two years for Association of international students. It\u2019s the same situation with other organizations, whether it\u2019s an international organization or Greek organizations. The difference that the domestic student groups may have a more supportive alumni culture who can assist financially. The International alumni are not willing to support events/food that is not fully representative of their culture in all aspects.
